(Please see Annexure F for Pie Chart/Bar Chart of Performance of 05 PEs against set indicators)

Analysis of Performance of 05 PEs against Set Indicators
The analysis of the 05 Procuring Entities (PEs) reveals a generally well-structured procurement system
with  strong  adherence  to  planning  benchmarks  and  minimal  incidence  of  disputes  or  complaints.
However, the review also identifies significant concerns in competition quality, inclusivity, and data
accessibility. A moderate 36.67% of tenders followed development partners’ rules by number. In terms
of competition, an average of 6.13 tender documents were issued per package and 4.3 tenders were
submitted, yet only 1.93 were responsive on average. Alarmingly, just 20.69% of tenders received three
or more responsive bids, reflecting subdued competitive participation.

Planning  efficiency  indicators  show  remarkable  consistency,  with  100%  of  tenders  and  contracts
aligned to the Annual Procurement Plan (APP), and an average contract value of BDT 32.76 lakh. This
suggests  disciplined  forecasting  and  procurement  execution.  Performance  efficiency  was  similarly
strong, with 96.67% of contracts completed within the original contract period. However, the absence
of  any  liquidated  damage  impositions  raises  concerns  over  lax  contract  enforcement.  Delays  in
disbursement  of  payments,  issuance  of  partial  payment  certificates,  and  payment  release  durations
could not be evaluated due to restricted access to system records. Notably, 16.67% of contracts were
revised, pointing to a moderate level of deviation from planned execution timelines and scopes.

No formal complaints were lodged by either tenderers or PEs, and there were no unresolved disputes
or  award  modifications.  While  this  could  indicate  smooth  implementation,  it  may  also  reflect
underutilization of complaint redress mechanisms. In terms of implementation efficiency, the contracts
saw a cumulative time overrun of 459 days and cost overrun of BDT 52.73 lakh across four contracts.
This reinforces the need for tighter contract management and proactive mitigation of delivery risks.
Accessibility  remains  a  challenge,  with  only  31.52%  of  tenders  deemed  responsive  and  just  10%
participation from women-owned businesses. Again, the absence of reliable data on registered women-
owned firms and regional tender concentration limits a thorough analysis of inclusion metrics.

From a market diversity perspective, procurement activities were heavily concentrated under the Open
Tendering  Method  (OTM),  which  accounted  for  83.33%  of  tenders—an  approach  that  promotes
transparency and fairness in public procurement. DAE’s procurement portfolio is primarily focused on
goods (56.67%), followed by works (30%), with limited involvement in consulting and non-consulting
services,  reflecting  the  operational  nature  and  functional  priorities  of  the  organization.  While  no
instances of fraud or corruption were reported, and only 3.45% of tenders involved single submissions,

Procurement Post Review of the procurement conducted in the FY 2023-24 by the Department of Agricultrual Extension

87

a noteworthy 51.72% of contracts were awarded based on single responsive bids. This pattern raises
valid concerns about the depth of competition and exposes potential vulnerabilities in achieving optimal
pricing and value for money.

The review concludes that the PEs performed well in planning compliance and timely contract delivery.
Nevertheless,  critical  areas  such  as  competitive  depth,  inclusive  participation,  and  complete  data
transparency  require  urgent  attention.  Addressing  these  gaps  would  significantly  strengthen  the
integrity and effectiveness of the public procurement process.

Procurement Post Review of the procurement conducted in the FY 2023-24 by the Department of Agricultrual Extension

88

3.15 Value for Money (VfM) Assessment

The Value for Money (VfM) assessment was conducted at the project level to evaluate how effectively
DAE deployed public resources across five major projects. The assessment was informed by field visits,
interviews with stakeholders and beneficiaries, and detailed reviews of 30 completed contracts, with
emphasis on the four pillars of VfM: economy, efficiency, effectiveness, and equity.

From an economy perspective, most contracts were awarded below official cost estimates, indicating
prudent budgeting and competitive pricing practices. However, in a few cases, significant deviations
from estimates raised concerns about the accuracy of cost forecasting, suggesting the need for improved
estimation methods to better align budgets with market realities.

In terms of efficiency, procurement processes generally followed legal frameworks, though delays were
noted  in  the  evaluation  phase  for  several  contracts—particularly  for  works.  While  some  projects
demonstrated timely delivery and payment, others experienced extended timelines in evaluation and
approval stages, pointing to inefficiencies in contract administration and oversight.

Regarding effectiveness, outputs such as supply of agricultural tools, training materials, ICT equipment,
and infrastructure upgrades were largely delivered as intended. However, gaps in competition, limited
supplier diversity (notably a dominance of Dhaka-based firms), and occasional time overruns indicate
areas where project implementation could be more robust. The low participation of regional suppliers
may also have constrained the projects’ broader development impact.

The equity dimension was partially addressed through regionally distributed implementation sites and
some inclusion of women and underserved farming communities. Yet, supplier concentration and low
responsiveness  in  many  tenders  reflect  persistent  challenges  in  fostering  inclusive  and  widespread
participation.

Overall, the VfM assessment finds that while DAE has made tangible progress in aligning procurement
activities with key VfM principles, there remain areas requiring systematic improvements—particularly
in estimation accuracy, competition enhancement, and timely procurement cycle execution.

Procurement Post Review of the procurement conducted in the FY 2023-24 by the Department of Agricultrual Extension

89

3.16 Summary of Findings

The findings have been systematically categorized into major as well as general observations, mapped
against the critical stages of the procurement and contract management lifecycle.

3.16.1 Procurement Opportunities
Procurement advertisements (IFT & REOI) complied with  guidelines of PPR-2008: Rule 90(2) (ka)
and e-GP guideline:  Cl. 3.5.1.2 & 3.5.1.3, with dissemination via e-GP platform, national newspapers
and DAE’s website.

According  to  PPR-2008:  Rule  90(2)(ka),  IFT  advertisements  are  required  to  have  a  wide  daily
circulation. All the reviewed contracts followed the rule for publishing; however, the concept of wide
circulation  appears  debatable.  Some  IFTs  were  published  in  newspapers  such  as  The  Daily  Desh
Rupantor,  Somoyer  Alo,  Banglar  Nabochetona,  Bangla  Navakantha,  The  Daily  Ajker  Probhat,  and
Bangladesher  Alo in  Bengali, and  The  Daily  Voice  of  Asia,  Daily  Industry,  and  The  Daily  Post  in
English (Annexure-G). While this practice is legally compliant, it raises concerns about whether the
spirit of "wide circulation" is consistently upheld.

Procuring Entities (PEs) under the Department of Agricultural Extension (DAE) select newspapers for
advertisement based on the list approved by the Department of Films and Publications. In practice,
selections were consistently made from the first 50 newspapers on that list. Consequently, newspapers
with  comparatively  modest  audience  reach  may  have  been  chosen,  potentially  limiting  the  overall
effectiveness of wide dissemination.

3.16.2 Performance Security
As per PPR-2008: Rule 27 (1), Schedule II, Performance security for Goods and Related Services is
10% of contract value. But in 03 Goods tenders under EIVTSP project, performance security was kept
at 5% of contract value (P2C2, P2C3 & P2C4). This is a clear violation of PPA-2006 & PPR-2008.
No  Performance  security  was  found  for  P5C5.  This  indicates  a  negligence  in  maintaining  proper
documentation.

As per PPR-2008: Rule 27 (6), for Works tender Performance security shall be valid for the period until
twenty-eight (28) days from the intended completion date. In P5C7,  the Performance security was not
valid up to the intended completion date.

According  to  Rule  27(7),  50%  of  the  original  performance  security  must  be  retained  as  a  new
performance  security  to  cover  the  Defect  Liability  Period  (DLP),  replacing  the  old  performance
security. No such practice was observed in any contracts.

As per ITT Clause (65.1) (PG3), the Performance Security must remain valid for at least twenty-eight
(28)  days  beyond  the  completion  of  the  Supplier’s  performance  obligations  under  the  Contract,
including any warranty obligations. However, the consultant observed that none of the performance
securities provided covered the warranty period and the additional 28 days as required.

Procurement Post Review of the procurement conducted in the FY 2023-24 by the Department of Agricultrual Extension

90

3.16.3 Insurance
As per GCC Clause (36.1) (PW3), The Contractor shall provide, in the joint names of the Procuring
Entity and the Contractor, insurance cover from the Start Date to the end of the Defects Liability Period,
in the amounts specified in the PCC for the following events which are due to the Contractor’s risks:

•
•
•

loss of or damage to the Works, Plant, and Materials;
loss of or damage to Equipment;
loss of or damage to property (except the Works, Plant, Materials, and Equipment) in
connection with the Contract;

No insurance related documents were found in 08 work contracts.

3.16.4 Conflict of Interest
In P5C7 tender, PE declared himself as Adjudicator. It may lead to a conflict of interest, compromising
impartiality in dispute resolution. An independent, neutral adjudicator is typically preferred to maintain
fairness. (Annexure-F).

3.16.5 Miscellaneous
Condition No. 2 of the work order for three contracts (P5C1, P5C2, and P5C3) states that if the supplier
fails  to  deliver  the  goods  within  the  stipulated  timeframe,  the  work  order  will  be  canceled  without
notice. Additionally, the Project Director reserves the right to issue a work order to another tenderer,
subject to a recommendation from the Tender Evaluation Committee (TEC).

This provision is fundamentally contradictory to established contract law principles, as it undermines
the contractual obligation to provide notice and an opportunity for remedy before contract termination.
(Annexure-F).

3.16.6 Procurement Plan
Annual Procurement Plans (APP) were prepared and approved in compliance as per PPR-2008, Rule
16 (4) (7). The majority of procurement activities adhered to planned timelines, reflecting systematic
efforts in planning.

3.16.7 Formation of Procurement Committees (TOC/TEC and OCEC)
Tender Opening Committees (TOC) and Tender Evaluation Committees (TEC) were formed following
Rule 7(1) & 8(1) of PPR & e-GP guideline: Appendix 2 of BPR and Rule8(1), Schedule II of PPR, &
e-GP  guideline:  Appendix  2  of  BPR  e-GP  guideline  respectively.  These  committees  maintained
compliance in terms of membership composition and operational procedures.

Official Cost Estimate was prepared by the Official Estimate Committee following PPR, 2008, Rule-
16(5) (5ka).

Procurement Post Review of the procurement conducted in the FY 2023-24 by the Department of Agricultrual Extension

91

3.16.8 Preparation of Tender and RFP Documents
Standard Tender Documents (STDs) issued by BPPA were used in Goods, Works and Service tenders.
Requests for Proposals (RFPs) were well structured and a reasonable submission time is offered to the
prospective consultants and service providers.

3.16.9 Submission of Tenders and Proposals
As per Rule 61(4), Schedule-II of PPR, the minimum days allowed for preparation and submission of
tender/ proposals varies between 14 days to 42 days depending on the type and the estimated value of
the procurement. Tender submission time is per the guideline of PPR-2008: Rule-61(4), Schedule II.

02 package were re-tendered (P5C3 & P5C7 due to non-responsiveness of all submitted tenders in the
first time), and 14 days was allowed for submission as per PPR-2008, Rule 61(4), Schedule II.

3.16.10 Tender and Proposal Opening
Tender openings were conducted in compliance with PPR, 2008, and e-GP guidelines with adequate
documentation and transparency.

3.16.11 Tender and Proposal Evaluation
Tender  evaluation  for  OTM,  National  is  acceptable  and  in  accordance  with  PPR,  2008,  and  e-GP
guidelines, all tenders were evaluated within the timeline as per PPR-2008: Rule 36 (6), Schedule -III,
except in 07 tenders (P1C5, P1C6, P4C1, P4C3, P5C2, P5C3 & P5C5).

As per Rule 72 (2) the submitted RFQs were evaluated on the day of submission. No RFQs deemed
non-responsive and no procurement proceedings became annulled.

3.16.12 Approval of Tenders and Proposals
All  tenders  were  approved  within the  timeline  as  per  PPR-2008:  Rule  36  (6),  Schedule  –III  except
(P2C4).  All  tenders  were  approved  by  the  authority  defined  in  the  Delegation  of  Financial  Power
(DoFP).

Procurement processing lag/lead-time were within the timeline as per PPR-2008: Rule 36(5) & (6),
Schedule -III, Part (ka).

3.16.13 Contract Value vs. Original Cost Estimates (OCE)
The majority of contracts were awarded at 5-20% below the original cost estimates, demonstrating cost
efficiency in procurement and the effectiveness of competitive bidding. This suggests that bidders were
willing to offer lower prices, possibly due to market competition or cost-saving opportunities in project
execution.

3.16.14 Contract Award
All contracts award were made within the initial tender/proposal validity period.

As per PPR-2008: Rule 37(1), 126 (3), all tenders' award notifications were published on the CPTU’s
website/PE’s website/others.

Procurement Post Review of the procurement conducted in the FY 2023-24 by the Department of Agricultrual Extension

92

3.16.15 Completion of Contract
Variation/Extra Work/Repeat/Additional Delivery Orders etc. were made in 05 contracts P4C1, P4C2,
P4C3, P4C5 & P4C6 as per PPR-2008: Rule-39(18), 78, 79, 80, Schedule II. All variations were made
due to increase of scope.

As per PPR-2008: Rule 39 & Rule 40, all contracts were executed within the contractual completion
period except 14 contracts (P1C2, P1C3, P1C4, P3C1, P3C2, P3C3, P4C1, P4C2, P5C1, P5C2, P5C3,
P5C5, P5C6 & P5C7). However, among 14 contracts time extension document was not found in 01
contract (P5C7).

As per PPR-2008: Rule-38(4), 38 (14), 39(27) and contract document, P5C7 was subjected to liquidated
damage but no liquidated damage was imposed and deducted from the contractor’s bill.

3.16.16 Contract Amendment
All  variation/additional  delivery  was  made  as  per  PPR-2008:  Rule-39(18),  78,  79,  80,  Schedule  II.
Variations were made in made in 05 contracts P4C1, P4C2, P4C3, P4C5 & P4C6.

3.16.17 Fraudulence and Corruption
No  direct  instances  of  fraudulence  or  corruption  were  identified  during  the  review.  However,
irregularities in bid submissions and evaluation processes indicated potential vulnerabilities.

3.16.18 Complaints, Appeals, and Contract Disputes
There  were  no  complaints,  appeals,  or  contract  disputes  recorded  during  the  procurement  process,
indicating strong governance and adherence to PPR, 2008. This reflects positively on the transparency
and accountability of the processes undertaken.

Procurement Post Review of the procurement conducted in the FY 2023-24 by the Department of Agricultrual Extension

93

Chapter 4

Recommendations & Conclusion

4.1 Recommendations

Based on the observations of the Procurement Post-Review, the reviewer would like to propose some
recommendations to enhance procurement efficiency, market participation, and compliance with PPR,
2008:

4.1.1 Contract Management

Compliance with Prescribed Performance Security Amounts: All Procuring Entities (PEs) should
strictly adhere to the performance security amounts specified in Rule 27(1), Schedule II of PPR-2008
to ensure consistency and risk coverage.

Retention and Extension of PS in Goods Contracts: PEs should retain performance security for the
full warranty period plus 28 days and ensure its validity is extended if the contract period is revised.

DLP  Coverage  of  PS  in  Works  Contracts:  In  works  contracts,  50%  of  the  original  performance
security should be retained as new security for the Defects Liability Period (DLP), replacing the initial
guarantee. DAE may instruct all PEs to institutionalize this requirement as a standard practice to ensure
continued contractual coverage during the DLP.

Monitoring of Contractual Insurance: PEs must ensure contractors submit the required insurance as
per GCC Clause 36.1. If not submitted, the PEs may proceed to arrange it directly, ensuring that the
contractor’s compliance with insurance obligations is duly verified.

Contract amendments, time extensions, and variation orders (VO) must comply with PPR-2008 rules
[Time Extension: Rule 39(3); VO: Rules 78, 79, 80].

4.1.2 Human Resources Development (HRD) Facilities and Number of Staff Trained in
Procurement

The consultant noted that some PEs could benefit from enhanced procurement knowledge. DAE, in
collaboration with BPPA, may consider offering a three-week public procurement training program for
its  officers  and  also  organizing  e-GP  and  procurement  contract  management  training  for  officers
involved in procurement.

Additionally, DAE may consider initiating a project focused on advanced studies in procurement and
supply chain management - such as MCIPS and MPSM qualifications - to enhance the capabilities and
professional development of its officers, in line with practices adopted by other government agencies.

Procurement Post Review of the procurement conducted in the FY 2023-24 by the Department of Agricultrual Extension

94

4.1.3 Strengthen Procurement Planning

Regularly update the Annual Procurement Plan (APP) during project implementation to accommodate
changes in requirements and ensure alignment with project goals.

4.1.4 Procurement Opportunities (Promote Wider Market Participation)
All PEs of DAE select newspapers from the list approved by the Department of Films and Publications.
As all choices were made from the top 50, some newspapers with limited audience reach may have
been selected, potentially reducing nationwide coverage effectiveness.

To enhance the effectiveness of advertisement reach, PEs may consider applying additional criteria—
such  as  circulation  volume,  regional  readership  strength,  and  target  audience  relevance—when
selecting newspapers from the approved list. This will help ensure that advertisements are placed in
widely-read publications, thereby improving visibility and ensuring broader nationwide coverage.

4.1.5 Enhancing Confidentiality and Reliability in Official Cost Estimates
Ensure  Official  Cost  Estimates  are  prepared  using  comprehensive  market  research  and  updated
benchmarks  to  enhance  accuracy  and  reliability  and  maintain  its  confidentiality  by  implementing
restricted access.

Conduct  periodic  reviews  of  cost  estimation  practices  to  identify  and  mitigate  recurring  issues  in
procurement planning.

4.1.6 Procurement Process

Procurement activities must adhere to PPR 2008 and e-GP timelines. DAE may guide PEs to manage
lead times effectively and complete processes within the stipulated timeframe.

Key e-GP documents must be kept in hard copy in procurement files to avoid loss due to staff changes
or technical issues like server crashes or account hacks.

All necessary documents should be maintained in each procurement file. Following Schedule 8 Part-A
[Rule 43 (4)] of PPR 2008 is recommended to avoid complications.

4.1.7 Tender Evaluation

Strict adherence to Schedule 3 (Part-A) of PPR 2008 is required for evaluation and approval. PEs should
maintain  a time  log to track  procurement  processing, as  outlined  in  Rule  8(17)(18)  and  Schedule  4
(Part-Ka, Kha, Ga) of PPR 2008.

To enhance the evaluation of consultancy firms, EoI and Technical Proposal Evaluation Reports should
clearly justify ratings with reference to sub-criteria. DAE may consider organizing training to improve
understanding of consultancy services and adopt best practices from other PEs.

Procurement Post Review of the procurement conducted in the FY 2023-24 by the Department of Agricultrual Extension

95

4.1.8 Timely Payment Processing

Establish  mechanisms  to  ensure  timely  processing  of  interim  payments  to  contractors,  addressing
approval bottlenecks and minimizing delays.

4.1.9 Document Management

DAE may advice to all PEs to systematically maintain all procurement-related documents — including
tender  notices,  evaluation reports,  approvals,  contracts,  payment records, and  any  other  documents,
strictly following the record-keeping requirements set out in Schedule VIII, Part (Ka) and Part (Kha)
of the Public Procurement Rules (PPR) 2008

4.1.10 Foster Regional Supplier Participation

Develop  policies  and  incentives  to  increase  the  participation  of  regional  suppliers  in  procurement
activities.

Consider reserving specific tenders for non-Dhaka-based contractors to diversify the supplier base and
enhance competition.

4.1.11 Post-contract review sessions for PE

DAE may consider organizing biannual post-contract review meetings for all Procuring Entities (PEs).
These sessions would serve as a structured platform to reflect on implementation challenges, share best
practices,  and  identify  opportunities  for  enhancing  contract  performance,  risk  management,  and
compliance with procurement regulations.

4.1.12 Ensure Governance and Transparency

Continue  efforts  to  maintain  zero  complaints,  appeals,  and  contract  disputes  by  upholding  strong
governance and accountability measures.

Regularly  review  procurement  processes  to  identify  and  address  procedural  weaknesses,  ensuring
adherence to PPR, 2008.

4.1.13 Establish a Dedicated Procurement Wing

DAE may establish a dedicated Procurement Wing to enhance institutional capacity in managing public
procurement.  This  unit  would  be  responsible  for  monitoring  procurement  performance,  evaluating
training needs, and overseeing high-value or complex procurement activities. Establishing such a wing
would promote greater compliance, efficiency, and strategic oversight across all procurement functions.

Procurement Post Review of the procurement conducted in the FY 2023-24 by the Department of Agricultrual Extension

96

4.2 Conclusion
The  Procurement  Post-Review  of  selected  projects  under  the  Department  of  Agricultural  Extension
(DAE) provides valuable insights into the effectiveness, transparency, and procedural compliance of
procurement practices. The review highlights commendable efforts by the Procuring Entities (PEs) in
adhering to the Public Procurement Act 2006 (PPA-2006) and Public Procurement Rules 2008 (PPR-
2008), particularly in the areas of cost estimation, tendering procedures, and contract execution. The
analysis revealed that most procurement activities were completed within budget, with minimal time
overruns, reflecting the operational efficiency and commitment of the implementing agencies.

However, the review also identifies critical areas that require strategic attention. Issues such as limited
market competition, high dependency on Dhaka-based suppliers, insufficient responsiveness to tender
advertisements,  and  fragmented  documentation  practices  suggest  the  need  for  further  institutional
strengthening. Additionally, the absence of access to the e-GP system and delayed data submission
constrained  the  review’s  depth.  To  address  these  challenges,  it  is  imperative  that  DAE  enhances
stakeholder  engagement,  fosters  capacity  development  in  procurement  management,  and  ensures
comprehensive documentation and archiving of contract records.

Looking  forward,  DAE’s  leadership  in  embracing  best  practices  and  promoting  a  culture  of
accountability and continuous improvement will be instrumental in driving procurement excellence.
Institutionalizing learnings from this review—through policy refinement, targeted training, and inter-
agency collaboration—will not only improve procurement performance but also reinforce public trust
in the efficiency and integrity of government spending.

Procurement Post Review of the procurement conducted in the FY 2023-24 by the Department of Agricultrual Extension

Comments and recommendations

The payments of bills were made in timely manner.

1.  PE complied with the procedures & guidelines according to PPA-2006 and PPR-2008.
2.  Actual days between opening and completion/submission of evaluation was  56 days against allocated

03 weeks as per PPR-2008: Rule36(6), Schedule -III.

3.  Procurement processing lag/lead-time (i.e. Days actual between opening and issuance of NOA/PO/LOI)

was 57 days against allocated 06 weeks as per PPR-2008: Rule36(5) & (6), Schedule -III, Part-1
4.  05 tenderers out of submitted 06 tenderers were technically non-responsive due to various reasons (ref.
5.4), which made only 01 tender technically responsive. PE should adopt a more prudent and thoughtful
approach  in  setting  'Qualification  Criteria'  to  ensure  that  a  greater  number  of  tenderers  become
technically responsive, thereby enhancing the competitiveness of the tender.

5.  Documentation was good.

Timeliness of payments to contractor

Comments and recommendations

The payments of bills were made in timely manner.
In practice, bills are paid only after receipt of funds, sometimes contractors submit prayers for bills.
B.  PE complied with the procedures & guidelines according to PPA-2006 and PPR-2008.
C.  Actual days between opening and completion/submission of evaluation was 56 days against allocated 03

weeks as per PPR-2008: Rule36(6), Schedule -III.

D.  Procurement processing lag/lead-time (i.e. Days actual between opening and issuance of NOA/PO/LOI) was

57 days against allocated 06 weeks as per PPR-2008: Rule36(5) & (6), Schedule -III, Part-1

E.  04 tenderers out of submitted 06 tenderers were technically non-responsive due to various reasons (ref. 5.4),
which made only 02 tender technically responsive. PE should adopt a more prudent and thoughtful approach
in setting 'Qualification Criteria' to ensure that a greater number of tenderers become technically responsive,
thereby enhancing the competitiveness of the tender.

F.  Documentation was good.
G.  Performance security was not extended despite time extension. Expire: 28-Mar-2024. Time Extension: 13-

Jun-2024.

Comments and recommendations

which made only 01 tender technically responsive. PE should adopt a more prudent and thoughtful approach
in setting 'Qualification Criteria' to ensure that a greater number of tenderers become technically responsive,
thereby enhancing the competitiveness of the tender.

D.  Documentation was good.
E.  Contractual completion date 23-Apr-2024 and time was extended up to 30-Jun-2024. Original Performance

security was valid up to 18-Jun-2024. Performance security was not extended.

F.  No insurance was implemented.

1.  08 Tender documents were sold and 06 tender documents were submitted. 02 tenders were automatically

2.  Actual days between opening and completion/submission of evaluation was 64 days against allocated 03

weeks as per PPR-2008: Rule36(6), Schedule –III.

3.  Procurement processing lag/lead-time (i.e., Days actual between opening and issuance of NOA/PO/LOI)

was 65 days against allocated 04 weeks as per PPR-2008: Rule36 (5) & (6), Schedule III, Part-1.

4.  PE complied with the procedures and guidelines of PPA-2006 & PPR-2008.
5.  Competition in procurement was good, but due to technically non-responsiveness, only 01 tender remained

to be evaluated financially.

6.  PE should adopt a more prudent and thoughtful approach in setting 'Qualification Criteria' to ensure that a
greater number of tenderers become technically responsive, thereby enhancing the competitiveness of the
tender.

7.  Documentation was good.

was 68 days against allocated 04 weeks as per PPR-2008: Rule36 (5) & (6), Schedule III, Part-1.

E.  PE complied with the procedures and guidelines of PPA-2006 & PPR-2008.
F.  Competition in procurement was good, but due to technically non-responsiveness, only 01 tender remained

to be evaluated financially.

G.  PE should adopt a more prudent and thoughtful approach in setting 'Qualification Criteria' to ensure that a
greater number of tenderers become technically responsive, thereby enhancing the competitiveness of the
tender.

H.  Documentation was good.

No. contract executed within budget.

Deficiencies/defects observed

Timeliness of payments to contractor

Comments and recommendations

The payments of bills were made in timely manner.
In practice, bills are paid only after receipt of funds, sometimes contractors submit prayers for bills.
B.  PE complied with the procedures & guidelines according to PPA-2006 and PPR-2008.
C.  Competition was absent, with only two tender documents sold and one tender submitted. As per PPR-2008,
Rule:  97(29)  and  97(30);  if  a  single  tender  is  submitted  and  deemed  responsive,  the  Procuring  Entity  is
obligated  to  proceed  with  contract  formation  subject  to  the  condition  that  the  PE  provides  a  satisfactory
explanation  to  the  Approving  Authority  regarding  the  acceptance  of  the  single  tender  (PPR-2008,  Rule
97(30). No such explanation was found. However,  such limited competition significantly undermines  the
principles of value for money, as it restricts competitive pricing and may not ensure the best use of  public
funds.

Procurement Post Review of the procurement conducted in the FY 2023-24 by the Department of Agricultrual Extension                                                    126

D.  The Work Order issued by the Procuring Entity lacked clarity regarding the exact quantity of  ginger tuber

(seeds) to be supplied, making it challenging for the consultant to ascertain the required number.

E.  The Work Order stipulated that the supply activities would be evaluated and monitored by the Project Office.
However, no supporting documentation was available to substantiate the execution of these monitoring and
evaluation processes.

F.  The documentation for this procurement process was found to be inadequate. The reviewer had to repeatedly
request the necessary documents, and despite multiple follow-ups, the Procuring Entity was unable to provide
all the required documentation.

Comments and recommendations

B.  PE  complied  with  the  procedures  &  guidelines  according  to  PPA-2006  and  PPR-2008,  except  for

performance security.
C.  Competition was moderate.

Procurement Post Review of the procurement conducted in the FY 2023-24 by the Department of Agricultrual Extension                                                    134

D.  The performance security for this tender was set at 5%, contrary to the requirement stipulated under PPR-
2008, Schedule II, Rule 27(1), which mandates a performance security of 10% for Goods. The tender
document did not provide a clear or justifiable explanation for the deviation in the performance security
requirement, resulting in non-compliance with PPR-2008 provisions.

E.  The Work Order issued by the Procuring Entity lacked clarity regarding the exact quantity of power sprayer
and electric saw to be supplied, making it challenging for the consultant to ascertain the required number.
F.  The Work Order stipulated that the supply activities would be evaluated and monitored by the Project Office.
However, no supporting documentation was available to substantiate the execution of these monitoring and
evaluation processes.

G.  The documentation for this procurement process was found to be inadequate. The reviewer had to repeatedly
request the necessary documents, and despite multiple follow-ups, the Procuring Entity was unable to provide
all the required documentation.

Comments and recommendations

The payments of bills were made in timely manner.
In practice, bills are paid only after receipt of funds, sometimes contractors submit prayers for bills.

B.  PE  complied  with  the  procedures  &  guidelines  according  to  PPA-2006  and  PPR-2008,  except  for

performance security.
C.  Competition was moderate.
D.  The performance security for this tender was set at 5%, contrary to the requirement stipulated under PPR-
2008,  Schedule  II,  Rule  27(1),  which  mandates  a  performance  security  of  10%  for  Goods.  The  tender
document  did  not  provide  a  clear  or  justifiable  explanation  for  the deviation  in  the  performance  security
requirement, resulting in non-compliance with PPR-2008 provisions.

E.  The Work Order issued by the Procuring Entity lacked clarity regarding the exact quantity of printer, router
and scanner to be supplied, making it challenging for the consultant to ascertain the required number.
F.  The Work Order stipulated that the supply activities would be evaluated and monitored by the Project Office.
However, no supporting documentation was available to substantiate the execution of these monitoring and
evaluation processes.

G.  The documentation for this procurement process was found to be inadequate. The reviewer had to repeatedly
request the necessary documents, and despite multiple follow-ups, the Procuring Entity was unable to provide
all the required documentation.

No. contract executed within budget.

Timeliness of payments to contractor

Comments and recommendations

The payments of bills were made in timely manner.
In practice, bills are paid only after receipt of funds, sometimes contractors submit prayers for bills.

B.  PE  complied  with  the  procedures  &  guidelines  according  to  PPA-2006  and  PPR-2008,  except  for

performance security.
C.  Competition was moderate.
D.  The performance security for this tender was set at 5%, contrary to the requirement stipulated under PPR-
2008,  Schedule  II,  Rule  27(1),  which  mandates  a  performance  security  of  10%  for  Goods.  The  tender
document  did  not  provide  a  clear  or  justifiable  explanation  for  the deviation  in  the  performance  security
requirement, resulting in non-compliance with PPR-2008 provisions.

E.  The  Work  Order  issued  by  the  Procuring  Entity  lacked  clarity  regarding  the  exact  quantity  of  desktop

computers to be supplied, making it challenging for the consultant to ascertain the required number.

Procurement Post Review of the procurement conducted in the FY 2023-24 by the Department of Agricultrual Extension                                                    150

F.  The Work Order stipulated that the supply activities would be evaluated and monitored by the Project Office.
However, no supporting documentation was available to substantiate the execution of these monitoring and
evaluation processes.

G.  The documentation for this procurement process was found to be inadequate. The reviewer had to repeatedly
request the necessary documents, and despite multiple follow-ups, the Procuring Entity was unable to provide
all the required documentation.

Comments and recommendations

D.  In contract agreement, there was typing error in the date of contract. It was typed 15th Day of November 2022
instead of 15th Day of November 2023. As this is the Contract Agreement, more care should be given to
prevent this kind of error.

E.  As per work order an Inspection Team finalized be Project Director, SACP supposed to inspect the goods

for conformity of specifications. No such team and inspection report were found.

SACP project has a web-based MIS to carry out a robust monitoring and evaluation system for
the SACP activities. As per GOB and IFAD requirements; mPower Social Enterprises Ltd. was
selected through a competitive tendering for the Phase I developer of the MIS. (Contract No:
12.01.0000.900.07.20-4341, Date: 25-Oct-202). Since the Phase II of the MIS development is
building up on the Phase I, to avoid delay in the development of upgraded MIS, SSS method
was selected and
mPower Social Enterprises Ltd. was called for negotiation meeting following submission of
RFP. After negotiation meeting (held on 01-Feb-2024), and getting no objection from IFAD
(Development Partner), proposal evaluation committee sent negotiation meeting minutes to
HOPE for approval.

Procurement Post Review of the procurement conducted in the FY 2023-24 by the Department of Agricultrual Extension                                                    261

Timeliness of payments to contractor

Comments and recommendations

The payments of bills were made in timely manner.
In practice, bills are paid only after receipt of funds, sometimes contractors submit prayers for bills.
D.  PE complied with the procedures & guidelines according to PPA-2006 and PPR-2008.
E.  Contractual completion date was 15-Apr-2023. According to completion certificate contract was completed
on 29-May-2023. Contract was overrun by 44 days. No time extension certificate was found. As there was
no time extension document, contractor was subject to [as per PCC (GCC 35.1)] liquidated damage, but no
liquidated damage was deducted.

F.  The performance security should have been valid for at least 28 days beyond the one-year warranty period;

however, it was only valid for five months after the contractual completion date.

Timeliness of payments to contractor

Comments and recommendations

The payments of bills were made in timely manner.
In practice, bills are paid only after receipt of funds, sometimes contractors submit prayers for bills.
B.  PE complied with the procedures & guidelines according to PPA-2006 and PPR-2008.
C.  Actual days between opening and completion/submission of evaluation took 79 days instead of 06 weeks.
D.  The performance security should have been valid for at least 28 days beyond the two-year warranty period;
however, it was only valid up to 19-Jul-2024, whereas it should be valid up to 26-May-2026. PE should take
this into consideration.

E.  In work order dated 01-Aug-2023, it was stated in condition no 3 (attached herewith) that if the supplier fails
to deliver the goods within the specified timeframe, the work order shall be canceled without prior notice.
This  provision  directly  contradicts  GCC  Clause  42  regarding  contract  termination.  It  was  also  stated  in
condition 3 that based on recommendations from the  TEC, the Procuring Entity (PE)  reserve  the right to
issue work order to another tenderer, which is also inconsistent with PPR-2008.

Time overruns

Cost overruns

Contract was overrun by 77 days

No. contract executed within budget.

Deficiencies/defects observed

No defect or deficiency was identified and observed.

Timeliness of payments to contractor

Comments and recommendations

The payments of bills were made in timely manner.
In practice, bills are paid only after receipt of funds, sometimes contractors submit prayers for bills.
B.  PE complied with the procedures & guidelines according to PPA-2006 and PPR-2008.
C.  The performance security should have been valid for at least 28 days beyond the two-year warranty period;
however, it was only valid up to 19-Oct-2024, whereas it should be valid up to 17-Apr-2026. PE should take
this into consideration.

D.  Original completion time of this contract was 69 days. Time was extended up to 02-Apr-2024 for 90 days.
As per PCC (GCC 34.4) if for time extension above 20% HOPE’s approval is required and time extension
shall be ratified by amendment of the contract. No such amendment was seen. This is a clear violation of the
tendering procedure.

E.  In work order dated 26-Oct-2023, it was stated in condition no 3 (attached herewith) that if the supplier fails
to deliver the goods within the specified timeframe, the work order shall be canceled without prior notice.

Procurement Post Review of the procurement conducted in the FY 2023-24 by the Department of Agricultrual Extension                                                    278

This  provision  directly  contradicts  GCC  Clause  42  regarding  contract  termination.  It  was  also  stated  in
condition 3 that based on recommendations from the TEC, the Procuring Entity (PE) reserve the right to
issue work order to another tenderer, which is also inconsistent with PPR-2008.

While the DAE has demonstrated a strong
commitment to achieving project objectives, a
few instances of non-compliance were
observed at the individual contract level and
from a broader perspective, the overall
performance of DAE across the reviewed
projects remains commendable. In response to
feedback from the Key Discussant, the
Consultant has revised the Executive Summary
to more accurately reflect both the
organization’s strengths and the areas requiring
attention, ensuring alignment with observed
project outcomes and stakeholder perspectives.

responsiveness

1.4  Data explanation
1,5  Reason of lack of competition

1.7  Explanation regarding managing works
contract at a value 10% less or more of
OCE

Complied
Complied
Complied (Section 3.7.1.3 Observations in
competition, Serial number 4)
As per Section 31(3) of the PPA-2006, in case
of works contracts under OTM and NCT, any
tender quoting a price that deviates by more
than ±10% from the Official Cost Estimate
(OCE) shall be considered non-compliant. In
accordance with this provision, a total of four
tenders were declared non-responsive—two in
Package P1C5 and two in Package P2C5. The
detailed justifications for these exclusions are
presented in Serial No. 5.4, Part-2:
Compliance with Act & Rules and
Guidelines (e-GP & DP’s) of the Contract
Annexure.

reasons, ensuring compliance with applicable
